<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en"><span dir="auto">Madonna albums discography</span></h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"></div>

<p>American singer <a href="/wiki/Madonna_(entertainer)" title="Madonna (entertainer)">Madonna</a> has released thirteen <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Studio_album" title="Studio album">studio albums</a>, six <a href="/wiki/Compilation_album" title="Compilation album">compilation albums</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Soundtrack_album" title="Soundtrack album">soundtrack albums</a>, four <a href="/wiki/Live_album" title="Live album">live albums</a>, 11 <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">extended plays</a>, three <a href="/wiki/Remix_album" title="Remix album">remix albums</a>, and 21 <a href="/wiki/Box_set" title="Box set">box sets</a>. In 1982, Madonna signed a recording contract with <a href="/wiki/Sire_Records" title="Sire Records">Sire Records</a>, a label owned by <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros._Records" title="Warner Bros. Records">Warner Bros. Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1"><a href="#cite_note-1"><span>[</span>1<span>]</span></a></sup> The first release under the label was her self-titled debut album, <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Madonna_(album)" title="Madonna (album)">Madonna</a></i> (1983).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-MetzBenson1999_2-0"><a href="#cite_note-MetzBenson1999-2"><span>[</span>2<span>]</span></a></sup> It peaked at number eight on the <a href="/wiki/Billboard_200" title="Billboard 200"><i>Billboard</i> 200</a> and was certified five times <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">platinum</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Recording_Industry_Association_of_America" title="Recording Industry Association of America">Recording Industry Association of America</a> (RIAA).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_3-0"><a href="#cite_note-us-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> She followed the debut album with the sophomore release, <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin" title="Like a Virgin">Like a Virgin</a></i> (1984). The album topped the chart in several countries and was certified diamond by the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_album)" title="True Blue (Madonna album)">True Blue</a></i> was released as her third studio album in 1986 and sold 25 million copies worldwide, while becoming her second chart topper in US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trueblue_5-0"><a href="#cite_note-trueblue-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1987, she released two albums that reached platinum status in the United States: the <i><a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(soundtrack)" title="Who's That Girl (soundtrack)">Who's That Girl soundtrack</a></i> and her first remix compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/You_Can_Dance" title="You Can Dance">You Can Dance</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rooksby2004_6-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rooksby2004-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's fourth studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(album)" title="Like a Prayer (album)">Like a Prayer</a></i> (1989), became her third number-one album on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, achieving quadruple platinum in US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-us_3-1"><a href="#cite_note-us-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna entered the 1990s with the release of the soundtrack, <i><a href="/wiki/I%27m_Breathless" title="I'm Breathless">I'm Breathless</a></i> (1990), which contained songs inspired by the film <i><a href="/wiki/Dick_Tracy_(1990_film)" title="Dick Tracy (1990 film)">Dick Tracy</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taraborrelli2002_7-0"><a href="#cite_note-Taraborrelli2002-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup> She also released her first greatest hits compilation, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Immaculate Collection</a></i>, in the same year. The album has sold more than 30 million copies, becoming the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_worldwide" title="List of best-selling albums worldwide">best-selling compilation album</a> by a solo artist.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-immaculate_8-0"><a href="#cite_note-immaculate-8"><span>[</span>8<span>]</span></a></sup> It also became the <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_albums_in_the_United_Kingdom" title="List of best-selling albums in the United Kingdom">second best-selling album</a> by a female artist in the United Kingdom and her second diamond album in the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-2"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ukbest_9-0"><a href="#cite_note-ukbest-9"><span>[</span>9<span>]</span></a></sup> In 1991, she signed a $60 million recording contract and business deal with Warner Bros. and <a href="/wiki/Time_Warner" title="Time Warner">Time Warner</a>. As part of this, she founded <a href="/wiki/Maverick_Records" title="Maverick Records">Maverick Records</a>, which became her main record company, with Sire and Warner Bros. as distributors of her music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> Her next releases under Maverick were the studio albums <i><a href="/wiki/Erotica_(Madonna_album)" title="Erotica (Madonna album)">Erotica</a></i> (1992) and <i><a href="/wiki/Bedtime_Stories_(Madonna_album)" title="Bedtime Stories (Madonna album)">Bedtime Stories</a></i> (1994), as well as <i><a href="/wiki/Something_to_Remember" title="Something to Remember">Something to Remember</a></i>, a collection of Madonna ballads. All of them reached multi-platinum status in the US and achieved commercial success.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-3"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Taraborrelli2002_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-Taraborrelli2002-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Univision_11-0"><a href="#cite_note-Univision-11"><span>[</span>11<span>]</span></a></sup> Her <a href="/wiki/Evita_(soundtrack)" title="Evita (soundtrack)">third soundtrack album</a>, from the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Evita_(1996_film)" title="Evita (1996 film)">Evita</a></i>, was released in 1996. The double-disc endeavor was certified five times platinum by the RIAA, recognizing 2.5 million shipments throughout the United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-4"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup> Madonna's seventh studio album, <i><a href="/wiki/Ray_of_Light" title="Ray of Light">Ray of Light</a></i>, was released in 1998 and has shipped around 20 million units worldwide.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-RayofLightsales_12-0"><a href="#cite_note-RayofLightsales-12"><span>[</span>12<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In 2000, <i><a href="/wiki/Music_(Madonna_album)" title="Music (Madonna album)">Music</a></i> became Madonna's fourth number-one album on the <i>Billboard</i> 200; it was her first number-one in 11 years, since <i>Like a Prayer</i>. It also topped the album charts of several European countries.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/American_Life" title="American Life">American Life</a></i> (2003) became Madonna's fifth <i>Billboard</i> 200 number-one album. However, it did not achieve multi-platinum status and became Madonna's lowest-selling studio album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-riaa1_4-5"><a href="#cite_note-riaa1-4"><span>[</span>4<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-telegraph_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-telegraph-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions on a Dance Floor</a></i>, released in 2005, was heralded as her comeback album, opening at number one in United States and in all major music markets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2007, Madonna signed a $120 million, 10-year business and recording <a href="/wiki/360_deal" title="360 deal">360 deal</a> with <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Live_Nation" title="Live Nation">Live Nation</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> Her remaining contract with Warner Bros. ended with her eleventh studio album <i><a href="/wiki/Hard_Candy_(Madonna_album)" title="Hard Candy (Madonna album)">Hard Candy</a></i> (2008), which became her seventh number-one album on the <i>Billboard</i> 200, and <i><a href="/wiki/Celebration_(Madonna_album)" title="Celebration (Madonna album)">Celebration</a></i> (2009), her third greatest hits compilation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2011, Madonna announced she had signed a three-album deal with <a href="/wiki/Interscope_Records" title="Interscope Records">Interscope Records</a>, who will distribute new recordings in partnership with Live Nation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> The first release from this deal was her twelfth studio album <i><a href="/wiki/MDNA_(album)" title="MDNA (album)">MDNA</a></i> (2012), which became her eighth chart topper in US.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Madonna has sold more than 300 million records worldwide and is recognized as <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists" title="List of best-selling music artists">the world's top-selling female recording artist of all time</a> by the <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup> She is ranked by the RIAA as the best-selling female rock artist of the 20th century and second <a href="/wiki/List_of_best-selling_music_artists_in_the_United_States" title="List of best-selling music artists in the United States">top-selling female artist in the United States</a>, with 64.5 million <a href="/wiki/RIAA_certification" title="RIAA certification">certified</a> albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup> Her albums <i>The Immaculate Collection</i>, <i>Like a Virgin</i> and <i>True Blue</i> are among the top 100 certified albums according to the RIAA.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United Kingdom, she has become the most successful solo artist with a total of 12 number-one albums.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup> According to <a href="/wiki/British_Phonographic_Industry" title="British Phonographic Industry">British Phonographic Industry</a> (BPI), Madonna is the most certified artist of all time in United Kingdom, with 45 awards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bpi_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-bpi-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p></p>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Studio_albums">Studio albums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Studio albums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>

<dt>Notes</dt>

<ul>
<li><b>A</b><span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_a1"><b><a href="#ref_note_a1">^</a></b></span> Germany sales figures of <i>Ray of Light</i> until December 1998.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-147"><a href="#cite_note-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>B</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_b1"><b><a href="#ref_note_b1">^</a></b></span> Standard worldwide: 1-CD. Standard USA: 2-CD (counted as double units). RIAA counts double albums twice towards certification if over 100 minutes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>C</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_c1"><b><a href="#ref_note_c1">^</a></b></span> Sales of 5,817,000 units does not include the sales of the album prior to May 25, 1991. After that, sales were tracked by <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a> across United States.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Billboard_.E2.80.93_Ask_Billboard_150-0"><a href="#cite_note-Billboard_.E2.80.93_Ask_Billboard-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>D</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_d1"><b><a href="#ref_note_d1">^</a></b></span> This EP is considered in some countries as a single and in others as an album.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-151"><a href="#cite_note-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li><b>E</b> <span class="citation wikicite" id="endnote_note_e1"><b><a href="#ref_note_e1">^</a></b></span> For accuracy in US sales of albums such as "Ray of Light". As of September 2011, the album has sold 3,900,000 copies in the U.S. according to <a href="/wiki/Nielsen_SoundScan" title="Nielsen SoundScan">Nielsen SoundScan</a>, which does not count albums sold through clubs like the BMG Music.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> Combined, it has sold over 4,359,000 copies in the U.S. with additional 459,000 copies sold at BMG Music Clubs.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BMG_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-BMG-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Limited_releases">Limited releases</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Limited releases">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Extended_plays">Extended plays</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Extended plays">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col" width="30%">Album details</th>
<th scope="col">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Like_a_Virgin_(song)" title="Like a Virgin (song)">Like a Virgin &amp; Other Big Hits!</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: October 10, 1984</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner-Pioneer Japan</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only EP released in 1984 by Warner-Pioneer Japan. Includes "Like a Virgin" (Extended Dance Remix), "Holiday", "Lucky Star" (Extended Dance Remix) and "Borderline" (Extended Dance Remix). It was later released as a CD maxi-single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-154"><a href="#cite_note-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>12"ers+2</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: September 6, 1985</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: Cassette</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Rare first <a href="/wiki/Extended_play" title="Extended play">EP</a> by Madonna. Its release was cancelled in 1985 by <a href="/wiki/Sire_Records" title="Sire Records">Sire Records</a>, but was later available in September 1985 as a promotional only cassette in Japan. The release was cancelled due to the relentless release schedule of Madonna products available in 1985 including the re-release of the albums <i>Madonna</i> and <i>Like a Virgin</i> in many territories. Tracklisting: "Ain't No Big Deal", "Dress You Up" (The 12" Formal Mix), "Angel" (Extended Dance Mix) "Lucky Star" (U.S. Remix), "Into the Groove", "Material Girl" (Jellybean Dance Mix), "Borderline" (U.S. Remix) and "Like a Virgin" (Extended Dance Remix).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Madonna Mix</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: 1985</li>
<li>Label: WEA · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: LP</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Rare Venezuelan vinyl EP released in 1985. Includes the tracks: "Borderline", "Holiday" and "Into the Groove" on Side A. "Angel", "Material Girl" and "Dress You Up" on the other side. All tracks are sequenced into each other, like a DJ set and are the original album versions. This set was also later released in Colombia and Ecuador.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_song)" title="True Blue (Madonna song)">Super Club Mix: True Blue</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: October 1986</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner-Pioneer Japan</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only EP released in 1986 by Warner-Pioneer Japan. Includes "True Blue" (The Color Mix), "Everybody" (Dub Version), "Papa Don't Preach" (Extended Remix), "Everybody" (Extended Version) and "Live to Tell" (Instrumental). It was later released as a CD maxi-single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/La_Isla_Bonita" title="La Isla Bonita">La Isla Bonita: Super Mix EP</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: May 25, 1987</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner-Pioneer Japan</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only EP released in 1987 by Warner-Pioneer Japan. Includes "La Isla Bonita" (Extended Remix), "Open Your Heart" (Extended Version), "Gambler", "Crazy for You" and "La Isla Bonita" (Instrumental). It was later released as a CD maxi-single.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Madonna 1983–1989</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: September 20, 1989</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japanese greatest hits EP released in September 1989 for DJs and retailers only. It was later re-released in May 1990 as <i>Madonna 1983–1990</i>, replacing the tracks "Crazy for You" and "Into The Groove" with "<a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue</a>" and "<a href="/wiki/Keep_It_Together_(Madonna_song)" title="Keep It Together (Madonna song)">Keep It Together</a>." <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton2002_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-Morton2002-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Vogue_(Madonna_song)" title="Vogue (Madonna song)">Vogue EP</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: September 25, 1990</li>
<li>Label: Sire · WEA Japan</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only EP released in 1990 by WEA Japan. Includes three remixes of "Vogue", two remixes of "Hanky Panky" and the album version of "More".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160"><span>[</span>160<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>It peaked at number 72 on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon_Albums_Chart" title="Oricon Albums Chart">Oricon Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161"><span>[</span>161<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection#The_Holiday_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Holiday Collection</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: June 2, 1991</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD · Cassette</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Limited edition UK EP to accompany the 1991 re-release of "<a href="/wiki/Holiday_(Madonna_song)" title="Holiday (Madonna song)">Holiday</a>" (1983). The EP includes three tracks omitted from <i>The Immaculate Collection</i> (1990), namely "<a href="/wiki/True_Blue_(Madonna_song)" title="True Blue (Madonna song)">True Blue</a>" (1986), "<a href="/wiki/Who%27s_That_Girl_(Madonna_song)" title="Who's That Girl (Madonna song)">Who's That Girl</a>" (1987) and "<a href="/wiki/Causing_a_Commotion" title="Causing a Commotion">Causing a Commotion</a>" (1987).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton2002_159-1"><a href="#cite_note-Morton2002-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Deeper_and_Deeper" title="Deeper and Deeper">Deeper and Deeper EP</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: April 10, 1993</li>
<li>Label: Maverick · Sire · Warner Music Japan</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only 12-track EP released in 1993 by Warner Music Japan. Includes six remixes of "Deeper and Deeper", "Bad Girl" (Extended Mix) and five remixes of "Erotica".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162"><span>[</span>162<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Rain_(Madonna_song)" title="Rain (Madonna song)">Rain EP</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: October 25, 1993</li>
<li>Label: Maverick · Sire · Warner Music Japan</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japan-only 10-track EP released in 1993 by Warner Music Japan. Includes three versions of "Rain", "Waiting" (Remix), "Up Down Suite" (Dub), "Bad Girl" (Extended Mix) and four remixes of "Fever".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163"><span>[</span>163<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
<li>It peaked at number 78 on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon_Albums_Chart" title="Oricon Albums Chart">Oricon Albums Chart</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164"><span>[</span>164<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: September 1993</li>
<li>Label: Warner Music Brazil</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Brazilian promotional EP to promote <a href="/wiki/The_Girlie_Show_World_Tour" title="The Girlie Show World Tour">The Girlie Show World Tour</a>. Includes the tracks "Erotica", "Deeper and Deeper", "Bad Girl", "Fever", "Rain" and "Bye Bye Baby". This release uses the same photography from the single release of the latter.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165"><span>[</span>165<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Remix_albums">Remix albums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Remix albums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col" width="30%">Album details</th>
<th scope="col">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Remixed_Prayers" title="Remixed Prayers">Remixed Prayers</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: August 23, 1989</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Japanese remix mini-album containing remixes of "<a href="/wiki/Like_a_Prayer_(song)" title="Like a Prayer (song)">Like a Prayer</a>" (1989) and "<a href="/wiki/Express_Yourself_(Madonna_song)" title="Express Yourself (Madonna song)">Express Yourself</a>" (1989) and different cover artwork by <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Ciccone" title="Christopher Ciccone">Christopher Ciccone</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Morton2002_159-2"><a href="#cite_note-Morton2002-159"><span>[</span>159<span>]</span></a></sup> It reached number 24 on the <a href="/wiki/Oricon" title="Oricon">Oricon</a> weekly albums chart and remained on the chart for five weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166"><span>[</span>166<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/GHV2" title="GHV2">GHV2 Remixed: The Best of 1991–2001</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: November 20, 2001</li>
<li>Label: Maverick · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: LP · CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Promo only remix album consisting of remixed tracks from <i>GHV2</i> (2001).</li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/Confessions_on_a_Dance_Floor" title="Confessions on a Dance Floor">Confessions Remixed</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: April 11, 2006</li>
<li>Label: Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: Triple LP</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Limited remixed vinyl edition accompanying <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i> (2005).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167"><span>[</span>167<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
</table>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_sets">Box sets</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Box sets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable plainrowheaders">
<tr>
<th scope="col" width="30%">Album details</th>
<th scope="col">Notes</th>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>True Blue/Like a Prayer</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: 1990</li>
<li>Label: Sire · <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">WEA Music Australia</a></li>
<li>Formats: Cassette</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Australian-only release with two albums on a single cassette. Uniquely, it includes the studio album <i>True Blue</i> on one side of the cassette and <i>Like a Prayer</i> on the other.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168"><span>[</span>168<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Royal Box</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: December 1990</li>
<li>Label: Sire · Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD · Cassette</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set version of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Immaculate_Collection" title="The Immaculate Collection">The Immaculate Collection</a></i> including a CD or cassette version of the album, postcards and a poster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169"><span>[</span>169<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>CD Single Collection</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: November 25, 1996</li>
<li>Label: Maverick · Sire · <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Japan</a></li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set of forty 3" CD singles, from "<a href="/wiki/Burning_Up_(Madonna_song)" title="Burning Up (Madonna song)">Burning Up</a>" (1983) to "<a href="/wiki/One_More_Chance_(Madonna_song)" title="One More Chance (Madonna song)">One More Chance</a>" (1996), in 8" × 8" × 4" deluxe black glossy box with red titles.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170"><span>[</span>170<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>The Immaculate Collection/You Can Dance</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: 1999</li>
<li>Label: <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">WEA Music</a>, <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music France</a></li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including the original album releases of <i>The Immaculate Collection</i> and <i>You Can Dance</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171"><span>[</span>171<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Ray of Light/The Immaculate Collection</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: 1999</li>
<li>Label: WEA Music, Warner</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set of <i>Ray of Light</i> and <i>The Immaculate Collection</i> released in New Zealand; also titled <i>Ray of Light (Special Edition)</i></li>
<li>Certified Gold by the RIANZ<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Scapolo_41-13"><a href="#cite_note-Scapolo-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172"><span>[</span>172<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>3 for One</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: October 31, 2000</li>
<li>Label: <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Australia</a></li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including the original album releases of <i>Madonna – The First Album</i> (1985 reissue), <i>Like a Virgin</i> (not including "<a href="/wiki/Into_the_Groove" title="Into the Groove">Into the Groove</a>") and <i>True Blue</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173"><span>[</span>173<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>

</ul>
</th>

<th scope="row"><i>American Life/Music/Ray of Light</i>

<li>Label: Warner Strategic Marketing · Warner Music France</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including the album release of <i>American Life</i>, the 11-track version of <i>Music</i> (with "American Pie" bonus track) and <i>Ray of Light</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-183"><a href="#cite_note-183"><span>[</span>183<span>]</span></a></sup> It charted at number 174 on the <a href="/wiki/Syndicat_National_de_l%27%C3%89dition_Phonographique" title="Syndicat National de l'Édition Phonographique">French Albums Chart</a> for two weeks.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-fra_32-4"><a href="#cite_note-fra-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>

<th scope="row"><i>Confessions on a Dance Floor: Special Edition Box</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: December 13, 2005</li>
<li>Label: Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including two books, one-month free membership to Icon (Madonna's official fanclub) and bonus track "Fighting Spirit".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-184"><a href="#cite_note-184"><span>[</span>184<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>The Complete Collection</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: August 2006</li>
<li>Label: <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music UK</a></li>
<li>Formats: CD · DVD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including all 17 albums and compilations from <i>Madonna</i> to <i>I'm Going to Tell You a Secret</i> (CD/DVD), the only album not included is the <i>Evita</i> soundtrack. Given as a promotional item to the media to celebrate the London leg of the <i>Confessions Tour</i> with only 100 copies made by Warner Music UK.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-185"><a href="#cite_note-185"><span>[</span>185<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Hard Candy: Limited Collector's Edition Candy Box</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: April 29, 2008</li>
<li>Label: Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set including the album with two bonus remixes of "4 Minutes" and a bag of peppermint candies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-186"><a href="#cite_note-186"><span>[</span>186<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Madonna: Dalle Origini Al Mito</i> <small>(<i>From the Beginning to the Myth</i>)</small>
<ul>
<li>Released: June 20 to August 29, 2008</li>
<li>Label: <a href="/wiki/Warner_Music_Group" title="Warner Music Group">Warner Music Italy</a></li>
<li>Formats: CD, DVD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Box set sold weekly by Italian newspaper <i>Corriere Della Sera</i> in 2008 which includes exclusive outer card sleeves design for each CD with Madonna logo spanning across the spines. Albums included were <i>Madonna</i>, <i>Like a Virgin</i> and <i>True Blue</i> (remastered versions), <i>Who's That Girl</i>, <i>Like a Prayer,</i> <i>I'm Breathless</i>, <i>Erotica</i>, <i>Bedtime Stories</i> and <i>Evita</i> plus two DVDs of <i>The Immaculate Collection</i> and <i>Ciao, Italia! – Live from Italy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-187"><a href="#cite_note-187"><span>[</span>187<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>Original Album Series</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: March 26, 2012</li>
<li>Label: Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>European 5-disc box set containing <i>True Blue</i> (remastered), <i>Like a Prayer</i>, <i>Ray of Light</i>, <i>Music</i> and <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-188"><a href="#cite_note-188"><span>[</span>188<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i><a href="/wiki/The_Complete_Studio_Albums_(1983_%E2%80%93_2008)" title="The Complete Studio Albums (1983 – 2008)">The Complete Studio Albums (1983 – 2008)</a></i>
<ul>
<li>Released: March 26, 2012</li>
<li>Label: Warner Bros.</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>Limited Edition European 11-disc box set containing <i>Madonna</i> (remastered), <i>Like a Virgin</i> (remastered), <i>True Blue</i> (remastered), <i>Like a Prayer</i>, <i>Erotica</i>, <i>Bedtime Stories</i>, <i>Ray of Light</i>, <i>Music</i>, <i>American Life</i>, <i>Confessions on a Dance Floor</i> and <i>Hard Candy</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-189"><a href="#cite_note-189"><span>[</span>189<span>]</span></a></sup> Sold 2,055 copies in the United Kingdom, debuting at number 70 on the Official Albums Chart.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-190"><a href="#cite_note-190"><span>[</span>190<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<th scope="row"><i>La Sélection Ideale: Madonna</i>
<ul>
<li>Released: August 13, 2012</li>
<li>Label: <a href="/wiki/Rhino_Entertainment" title="Rhino Entertainment">Rhino</a> · WEA Music · Warner Music France</li>
<li>Formats: CD</li>
</ul>
</th>
<td>
<ul>
<li>French box set digi-pak containing the remastered versions of <i>Madonna</i>, <i>True Blue</i> (but omits the bonus extended remixes found on the normal releases) and <i>American Life</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-191"><a href="#cite_note-191"><span>[</span>191<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
</td>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Footnotes">Footnotes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Madonna_albums_discography&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Footnotes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
